An Accidental Entrepreneur’s Journey

The inspiring journey of entrepreneurship and
philanthropy by founder and CEO Emeritus of
MSI
For over four decades, Manu Shah has exempli ed the quintessence of the
American Dream, transforming adversity into opportunity with unparalleled
vision and determination. An immigrant who arrived in the United States with
little more than ambition and a desire to succeed, Manu's journey from a
modest upbringing in Mandvi, Gujarat, to the helm of M S International, Inc.
(MSI) is a testament to the power of perseverance, adaptability, and strategic
foresight.
In his memoir, Life and Times of Manu Shah, Manu o ers an intimate glimpse
into his life's pivotal moments—his early days at Purdue University, the
foundational years of MSI, and the groundbreaking contract to supply black
granite for the Vietnam Veterans Memorial. With every chapter, he reveals the
strategic decisions and core values that propelled MSI from a small home-based
business to a global leader in the stone and surfaces industry.
Manu's narrative is rich with lessons on leadership, resilience, and innovation.
He re ects on the challenges of navigating cultural shifts, economic downturns,
and industry evolutions, sharing insights that are as profound as they are
practical. His story is not just about building a successful company; it is about
fostering a culture of integrity, continuous learning, and unwavering
commitment to excellence.
Manu Shah's remarkable achievements have been recognized with numerous
prestigious awards, including the Ernst & Young Entrepreneur of the Year
Award (2007), Corporate Citizen of the Year Award (2022) from the City of
Orange, Top 100 Philanthropy Leaders of the Global Indian Diaspora, and the
Distinguished Alumni Award from Purdue University. His innovative approach,
often described as "high-tech in low-tech," and his ability to leapfrog traditional
methods have left an indelible mark on the industry. Moreover, his profound
social impact—touching millions of lives, one life at a time—stands as a
testament to his dedication to making the world a better place.

ff

fi

fl

Life and Times of Manu Shah is more than a memoir. It is an inspiring blueprint
for entrepreneurs and leaders, a call to embrace challenges with courage, and a
celebration of the enduring impact of a visionary leader who continues to
shape the world of business with his ingenuity and heart.

Preface
This is a biography of Manu Shah, documenting his life
and times with his life partner Rika, and their journey in
America. Written primarily in the third person by Manu,
with the help of ChatGPT, it captures a series of stories
re ective of Manu and Rika's memories. This work has been
coordinated with Bhavik Muni,
Jasmin Sharma and
Bhavana Shah, serving as Social Impact Director, assisting
the Shah family with their philanthropic endeavors.
Manu Shah’s story is the quintessential American Dream.
Arriving in the United States in the late 1960s with a mere
$210 in his pocket and a borrowed $2,000, Manu
epitomized the spirit of relentless ambition. Graduating
with Honors from Purdue University in under a year, he
navigated the challenges of a new culture, language
barriers, and the competitive landscape of the American
job market with unparalleled determination and
adaptability to New Country.
Warren Bu et once said, "Someone's sitting in the shade
today because someone planted a tree a long time ago."
Manu’s journey embodies this sentiment. From declining a
coveted position at IBM to immersing himself in a smaller
company where he could learn every facet of the business,
Manu’s choices were always guided by a deep desire to
understand and master his environment. His early years in
America were marked by tireless e orts, working as a

ff

ff

fl

I

project engineer by day and building the foundation of his
own company by night.
Together with his wife, Rika, Manu laid the groundwork
for MSI in 1975 from their modest two-bedroom home.
Rika, balancing her role as a mother and a budding
entrepreneur, worked alongside Manu to grow MSI into a
leading company. Their biggest breakthrough came with
the contract to supply black granite for the Vietnam War
Memorial in 1981—a pivotal moment that solidi ed MSI’s
place in the industry.
Howard Schultz, the former CEO of Starbucks, once
noted, "In life, you have to take risks." For Manu and Rika,
the risk was monumental, but failure was never an option.
Today, MSI stands as a testament to their hard work,
employing thousands and supporting countless jobs
globally. With over 60 branches across North America and
a strong presence in India, MSI has become a beacon of
excellence in the industry, making dream surfaces
attainable for homes and o ces worldwide.
Manu never wanted to be Entrepreneur nor did know
what it means to be called “Entrepreneur”. Manu being
engineer and wanted to use Technolo y in his job, at home
or developing his wife Rika’s Export-Import business MSI.
Manu accidentally and unknowingly became Entrepreneur.
Rika’s vision for Manu must use his technical prowess in
low tech business as Natural stone for Memorial and later
for homes.
This biography captures the essence of Manu Shah’s life—
an entrepreneurial journey marked by resilience, hard

fi

g

ffi

II

work, and a steadfast belief in the power of dreams. It is a
story of how one man’s vision and a family's unwavering
support turned a small business into a thriving empire. As
you turn these pages, you will witness the evolution of a
dream into reality, driven by passion and a relentless
pursuit of excellence.
In keeping with Manu’s thirst for new technolo y, this
biography will be entirely online, interactive, and everevolving. It will feature photos, video links, presentations,
links to news and press updates, and audio for every
chapter, with translations in Spanish, Hindi, and Gujarati.
There will be no printing, no publisher, and no ghostwriter
—just an ongoing, never-ending story.
Here are Strengths in this Biography
Strengths
Authenticity and Personal Connection: The biography
is highly personal, o ering insights into not just Manu's
business journey but also his values, upbringing, and family
life. This authenticity adds a layer of relatability and
emotional depth, which is often missing in more corporatefocused biographies.
Lessons for Entrepreneurs: There are clear, actionable
lessons for young entrepreneurs, especially about building
a business from scratch, facing adversities, and maintaining
integrity in business. Manu's emphasis on the no-layo
policy and philanthropy adds a distinctive dimension not
commonly found in many biographies.

IV

Purpose of the Book
Introduction
The decision to write this biography stems from a deep
desire to document and share the journey of Manu and
Rika Shah. This book is not just a record of events but a
comprehensive guide that encapsulates the values,
principles, and lessons learned over a lifetime. It serves
multiple purposes: preserving family history, inspiring
entrepreneurs, guiding future leaders at MSI, and
promoting philanthropy.

1. Preserving Family History and Legacy
The Shah family story is one of resilience, education, and
cultural heritage. Spanning 14 generations, this biography
captures the essence of their journey from postindependence India to global business prominence. It
delves into the rich history, the struggles, and the values
that have been the foundation of Manu and Rika's lives.
Family Heritage: The book o ers insights into the family's
roots and the guiding principles that shaped Manu and
Rika's decisions.
Educational Journey: It chronicles Manu's academic
pursuits at VJTI and Purdue, highlighting the importance of
education in his success.
Founding of MSI: The narrative details the challenges

ff

V

faced in establishing MSI, emphasizing the partnership
between Manu and Rika as the cornerstone of the
company’s success.
Publishing this biography ensures that future generations
understand their heritage and the legacy they inherit,
o ering a source of inspiration and guidance.

2. Lessons for Aspiring Entrepreneurs
Manu's entrepreneurial journey is rich with lessons for
those aspiring to build their own businesses. One of the key
takeaways is the importance of self-reliance and avoiding
the pitfalls of relying on "Other People’s Money" (OPM).
Entrepreneurial Lessons: Success doesn’t come from
shortcuts or external investors but from calculated risks,
reinvesting pro ts, and staying true to core values.
Innovation in Low-Tech Industries: By leveraging hightech solutions in a traditionally low-tech industry, Manu
demonstrates the power of innovation.
Strategic Growth: The book provides a roadmap for
building a sustainable business without compromising on
values.
This biography serves as a beacon for aspiring
entrepreneurs, o ering practical advice and inspiration to
pursue their dreams with integrity.

Leadership Expectations: The book sets clear
expectations for MSI’s leaders, emphasizing ethical

MSI Commandments: It provides a detailed account of
MSI's guiding principles, such as the no-layo policy and

Organizational Culture: By sharing MSI's growth story,
the biography reinforces the importance of maintaining a

This biography will be an invaluable tool for MSI leaders,

4. Promoting Philanthropy and Social Impact
Philanthropy has always been a cornerstone of Manu and

This biography is more than a recounting of events—it’s a

VIII

How to Read Life and Times
of Manu Shah
This biography presents the extraordinary life and career
of Manu Shah, a visionary entrepreneur who transformed
challenges into opportunities. His story is not only about
building a successful business but also about creating a
lasting impact on employees, communities, and the global
market. The lessons within are relevant for individuals at
any stage of life, whether you are a student, an
entrepreneur, or a seasoned leader.
Here’s our guidance to readers on how to approach this
biography and what unique insights they can draw from
Manu's remarkable journey.

Key Lessons to Take Away from the Book
1. Adaptability and Resilience
M a nu S h a h’s j o u r n e y f ro m I n d i a t o A m e r i c a
demonstrates the importance of adapting to new
environments and overcoming adversity. Whether it’s
market changes or global disruptions, resilience is a
recurring theme throughout Manu's life. Readers will learn
how to embrace change and persist through di cult times,
lessons that are applicable in both business and personal
life.

ffi

IX

In an era where quick gains often overshadow ethics,
Manu Shah’s commitment to doing business the right way
sets a high standard. His insistence on avoiding
underhanded practices—even when competitors engaged in
unethical behavior—underscores the importance of
maintaining integrity for long-term success. His ethical
approach, from how MSI treated its employees to its global
supply chain, provides a roadmap for business leaders
seeking sustainable success.
3. Long-Term Vision and Strategic Thinking
The ability to think ahead, anticipate market changes,
and stay focused on long-term goals is a major theme in this
biography. Manu Shah's decisions were driven by bigpicture thinking, whether it was adopting new technologies
or expanding MSI into new global markets. Readers will
nd valuable insights into how long-term vision drives
consistent growth, even in unpredictable environments.
4. Employee and Community-Centric Leadership
One of the most unique aspects of Manu’s leadership is
MSI’s "No Layo Policy," which re ects his deep
commitment to employee welfare. His belief that
employees are the backbone of any business led to policies
that fostered loyalty and long-term growth. Furthermore,
his philanthropic work through the Sarva Mangal Family
Trust emphasizes giving back to society, inspiring readers

to consider how businesses can impact communities
positively.
5. Balancing Family, Business, and Philanthropy
Manu and Rika Shah's ability to balance growing a
multinational business while raising a family highlights the
importance of maintaining strong family values alongside
business success. This biography o ers lessons on how they
passed their values on to their children, ensuring that the
next generation of leaders continued the family’s legacy of
ethical leadership and social responsibility.

The Unique Lessons from Manu Shah’s
Biography
Unlike other entrepreneurial biographies, "Life and
Times of Manu Shah" presents a set of lessons that are
rarely found in stories of business leaders. Here are ve
distinctive takeaways:
1. No Layo
Security

Policy: A Commitment to Employee

Manu Shah’s principle of never laying o employees,
even during economic downturns, is a rare practice in the
business world. This commitment emphasizes that a
company's most valuable asset is its workforce, and
protecting them leads to long-term loyalty and success.
Lesson: Employee security fosters a loyal, dedicated
workforce, even when faced with nancial challenges.

fi

ff

ff

fi

ff

XI

Contrary to the all-or-nothing approach seen in many
entrepreneurial stories, Manu’s philosophy centers on
building a safety net before taking major risks. Whether it
was maintaining a steady job while starting MSI or planning
strategic exits, Manu understood that calculated risk-taking
requires a solid foundation.
Lesson: Successful entrepreneurs take risks, but they
also prepare safety nets to protect against failure.
3. Staying Under the Radar in Competitive Markets
One of the lesser-known strategies Manu employed was
growing MSI quietly in underdeveloped markets before
entering highly competitive industries. This lesson of
strategic discretion—focusing on overlooked opportunities
before facing larger competitors—is a unique business tactic
that stands out in his story.
Lesson: Growth can be achieved by staying out of the
spotlight and focusing on underdeveloped opportunities
rst.
4. Building True Partnerships with Suppliers
Manu didn’t view his supply chain as just a series of
transactions but as long-term partnerships. His strate y of
nancially supporting suppliers and fostering mutual
growth highlights a unique approach to business

fi

fi

2. The Importance of a Safety Net in
Entrepreneurship

relationships, one that is rarely discussed in business
literature.
Lesson: Treating suppliers as partners rather than
vendors creates lasting relationships that bene t both
parties.
5. Embedding Adaptability in Company Culture
While adaptability is often a trait attributed to individual
leaders, Manu ensured that his entire organization was
adaptable. By embedding exibility into MSI's core
operations, he built a company that could not only survive
but thrive in changing markets.
Lesson: Long-term success requires not just individual
adaptability, but creating a culture where the entire
organization can pivot and evolve.

1.1
Foreword - From History
Reader to History Maker

s a teenager, Manu's deep fascination with history
led him to explore not only the events of the past
but their geographic contexts, often connecting them to his
growing desire to come to America. History was more than
just stories of wars and empires; it was a window into
di erent cultures, economic movements, and the evolution
o f s o c i e t i e s . M a nu’s c u r i o s i t y a n d p a s s i o n f o r
understanding the world beyond his own led him to dream
of a life in America, a place he saw as a symbol of progress
and endless possibilities.
By his twenties, Manu had transformed from a history
enthusiast into a history storyteller. His ability to relate
historical lessons to present-day situations became a
signature part of his conversations, with the refrain
"History repeats itself" often shaping his thoughts. He
became known among his peers for drawing parallels
between past events and the contemporary world, o ering
wisdom grounded in historical perspective. Manu’s skill as
a speaker blossomed during this time, and he honed it
through Toastmasters International, where he became a

ff

ff

2

respected voice in his community, known for speeches that
blended history with modern-day insights.
As the years passed and Manu entered his thirties and
forties, his engagement with history deepened further. He
began documenting his thoughts through notes and essays,
often infusing them with historical context. These writings
re ected his belief in the power of understanding the past
to guide the future. It was during this period that Manu
realized something profound: through all his e orts in
America, he wasn’t just learning history; he was making
history in his own small way. As MSI grew and ourished,
Manu understood that his journey was one that deserved to
be recorded—not just as a personal story but as part of a
broader legacy. It was time to write his own history, a story
of resilience, growth, and the power of lessons from the
past shaping a remarkable future.

1.2
Introduction: American
Dream Forged into Reality
This chapter tells the story of Manu Shah, an immigrant from
India who arrived in the U.S. with little money but big dreams. After
graduating from Purdue University, Manu turned down a
prestigious job at IBM, choosing to work at a smaller company to
gain broader business experience. He later married Rika, and
together they founded MSI, starting from their home.
MSI grew from a small tech business into a major player in the
construction industry, with a breakthrough moment supplying
granite for the Vietnam War Memorial. Today, MSI is a successful
family-owned company, led by their sons, Raj and Rup. The story
showcases how hard work, determination, and smart decisions can
turn dreams into reality.

n the late 1960s, a
young engineer
named Manu Shah
arrived at Purdue
U n i v e r s i t y i n We s t

opportunities in a land
far from home. With just

daunting as it was hopeful. By 1967, America was in the
throes of the Vietnam War and the thrilling space race to
the moon. Amidst these monumental events, industries
across the nation desperately sought engineers, as many
American engineers joined defense corporations or were
swept up by NASA’s ambitious projects.
Graduating with honors in under a year from Purdue,
Manu faced a pivotal decision with three job o ers on the
table. As an immigrant in America, Manu’s challenges were
manifold—his stature was small at 5 feet 3 inches, he
weighed only 97 pounds, and he had already lost 9 pounds
due to the rigorous demands of his studies. Yet, what he
might have lacked in physical presence, he made up with a
bright mind and a relentless spirit.

to learn every facet of a
business, not just the engineering side. His decision to join
a smaller company accelerated his personal growth and
learning while receiving leadership opportunities at the
very beginning of his career. Later, he joined International
Harvester as a Project Engineer.
Four years later, Manu returned to India, where he
married Rika, a teacher of math and science from Mumbai.
Together, they embarked on a new journey, settling in Fort
Wayne, Indiana. While Manu honed his skills as a project
engineer at International Harvester(Now International
Trucks), Rika was an educator having experience in
teaching high school students in India. She landed a job as
a substitute teacher in a high school in Fort Wayne;
however, things did not go as planned. She encountered
the stark di erences in educational culture and respect for
teachers between America and India. She was quite clear;
she wouldn’t continue teaching and would rather focus on
something that gave her happiness and ful llment. After
becoming a mother, Rika’s path took a new turn as she
founded MSI from their two-bedroom home. By day, she

fi

ff

6

was a devoted mother; by night, she transformed into a
savvy businesswoman, with Manu by her side after hours.
Upon the birth of their second son, Rup, they moved into a
small house with a rather big basement – where their
business activities took place for the next 8 years – growing
kids while expanding the business.
MSI began as a modest venture, dealing initially in
integrated circuits and memory chips, but it was not long
before the business expanded into importing black granite
blocks and monuments. A pivotal moment came in 1981
when MSI secured a contract to supply black granite for the
Vietnam War Memorial. This project, fraught with risks,
was a turning point, propelling MSI towards a target of one
million dollars in revenue and prompting Manu to leave his
job to focus entirely on MSI.
Today, more than half a century later, MSI is a leading
name in the distribution of countertops, oor and wall
tiles, and outdoor hard surfaces. With over 3,000
employees across North America and an additional 750 in
India, MSI sources materials from 35 countries and
operates over 60 branches in major metropolitan areas.
The company not only beauti es homes and o ces but also
supports around 400,000 jobs in rural areas globally. Still a
family-owned enterprise with no plans to go public, MSI
stands as a testament to the enduring American dream, a
dream that Manu and Rika Shah, together with their sons
Raj and Rup, now CO CEOs, continue to build upon.
This is their American story—of dreams, struggles, and
unwavering perseverance—a narrative that underscores the

Historical Context
1. The Vietnam War and Economic Opportunities
(1960s-1970s): Manu Shah arrived in the U.S. during a time when
the Vietnam War was creating a high demand for engineers. Many
American engineers were recruited by defense companies or NASA,
opening opportunities for immigrants like Manu to ll the gap in
industries across the U.S. This economic environment played a
signi cant role in helping Manu secure job o ers and establish
himself in his new country.

2. The Space Race and Technological Advancements: In
the 1960s, America was competing with the Soviet Union in the race
to the moon. This era of rapid technological advancements meant
that industries were seeking innovative minds. Manu’s decision to
join a smaller company to learn multiple facets of business was a
strategic move that aligned with the growing demand for skilled
engineers and leaders who could navigate a rapidly evolving
industrial landscape.
Cultural Context
1. Entrepreneurial Spirit of the American Dream: Manu
and Rika’s journey of founding MSI exempli es the American
Dream, where immigrants with limited resources can build a
successful business through hard work and resilience. Their story
resonates with the core American value that anyone, regardless of
background, can achieve success if they persevere.
2. Balancing Family and Business: Rika’s role in building
MSI while raising children re ects the cultural shift in America
toward supporting women entrepreneurs. Her transition from
teaching to becoming a businesswoman highlights the adaptability
and determination required to balance family life with
entrepreneurial ambitions, a central theme in many immigrant
success stories.
3. Immigrant Contributions to U.S. Business: Immigrants
like Manu and Rika have played a crucial role in driving innovation
and creating jobs in America. MSI’s success, from importing granite
for the Vietnam War Memorial to becoming a major player in the
construction industry, underscores the signi cant impact that
immigrant-owned businesses have had on the U.S. economy.

Rika - The Unsung Heroine
Behind MSI
Rika Shah, co-founder of MSI and wife of Manu Shah, played a
key role in building the company. Raised in a large family in
Matunga, she brought her values of compassion and community to
both her family and business. After moving to the U.S., Rika
balanced raising their sons with helping grow MSI from their home.
Her leadership shaped MSI’s family-focused culture and guided
its growth into a global company. Rika also champions cause like
tobacco de-addiction and supports women’s empowerment through
charity work.
Rika remains the strong matriarch of the family, a vital force
behind MSI’s success.

DNA of the Shah Foundation
This chapter explores the roots of Manu Shah's entrepreneurial
spirit, tracing it back to his father, Ravilal Makanji Shah. Ravilal’s
journey from Kutch, Gujarat, to Mombasa, Kenya, showcases
resilience and a commitment to community service. After moving
back to India during World War II, Ravilal’s family settled in
Mumbai, where Manu was born. Growing up in a modest home,
Manu learned lessons of perseverance, independence, and
resourcefulness, which later shaped his leadership at MSI.
Before Manu Shah's entrepreneurial journey and the success of
MSI, there was a story of resilience and determination that began
with his father, Ravilal Makanji Shah.

From Kutch to Mombasa: Ravilal's Early
Adventures
Ravilal Lost his Father at 14; Completed Education in
English; The year was 1918, and young Ravilal Makanji Shah,
merely 16, faced the harsh reality of life in Kutch, Gujarat—a
region scant in rainfall and opportunities. The desert
community of Kutch o ered little to its youth, prompting
many, like Ravilal, to seek fortunes
beyond the familiar horizons.
With the British Empire's
expansive reach into Africa,
opportunities beckoned young
adventurers from India to its
colonies, where white-collar jobs
were abundant compared to the
subcontinent's limited prospects.

After brief stints in Seychelles and Zanzibar, Ravilal found
his footing in Mombasa by 1920. While From Mombasa a

a young girl from Mundra – 15 years old, in 1922, and in

World War II and Return to Kutch

Manu, age 2

Age 8

Age 12

The onset of World War II in 1939 brought turmoil and the
threat of German advances into East Africa by 1941. The
18

British government's call to arms for all able-bodied men
under 45 meant that Ravilal had to make a monumental
decision. With eight children to consider, he and Rambha
chose to return to their native Mandvi in 1942, undertaking
a perilous 22-day boat journey amidst the ongoing war.
Choosing not to return to Africa after the war, Ravilal’s
family resettled in Mandvi where they faced numerous
challenges. It was here, in this setting of renewed
beginnings, that Manu Shah was born on June 15, 1945, as
the ninth child—a peace baby symbolizing new hopes.

A New Start in Mumbai
The post-war years saw the marriage of Manu's three
elder sisters in Kutch, while Ravilal explored new
opportunities in Mumbai. By 1951, the family moved to the
new suburb of Ghatkopar, where young Manu commenced
his educational journey, surrounded by a melting pot of
cultures and ideas in India's burgeoning metropolis.
Rambha, balancing the demands of a large family,
instilled in Manu the virtues of perseverance and optimism.
"Never give up, never cry—there will be a better tomorrow,"
she would say, a mantra that deeply in uenced Manu's
early childhood development (ECD). From his siblings,
Manu learned the value of independence, a trait echoed
through the family’s ethos.
Living in a modest 390 square foot home taught Manu
invaluable lessons in space utilization—a skill that later
proved essential in managing MSI’s expansive inventory.
Furthermore, the diverse personalities within his own

Lessons for a Lifetime
As Manu grew, so did his responsibilities and his
understanding of the world around him. The collective
input from his family not only shaped his character but also
equipped him with the skills necessary to thrive in diverse
environments—be it in the educational pursuits in America
or the competitive business landscapes he would later
conquer.
This chapter of Manu Shah’s life provides insight into the
resilience, community service, and family values that
in uence his approach to business and life. It shows how
the challenges faced by the Shah family shaped their
journey, contributing to the growth and success of MSI and
its impact on the community today.

Manu’s Mother Rambhaben
This chapter highlights the deep in uence of Manu Shah's mother,

raised nine children and was known for her warmth, hospitality,

life lessons, where she taught patience, perseverance, and balance
through her cooking. Her skills as a seamstress, her frugality, and
her love for storytelling left a lasting impact on her family. Despite
lacking formal education, she was a spiritual woman, drawing
wisdom from Jainism. Her legacy of love, strength, and generosity
continues to guide her family.

1.6
Early Childhood Development
This chapter emphasizes the importance of the rst six years of a
child’s life, where rapid brain development occurs, laying the
foundation for future learning, behavior, and health. For Manu
Shah, growing up in Mandvi, Kutch, his early childhood was shaped
by his large family, particularly his older siblings who nurtured his
cognitive and emotional development in the absence of formal
daycare. This supportive environment fostered adaptability and
innovation, qualities that would later contribute to Manu’s success
as an entrepreneur.
The chapter also highlights Manu's involvement with Rocket
Learning, a nonpro t focused on early childhood education for
underserved children in India. The lessons from Manu's childhood
continue to in uence his commitment to supporting quality
education and early development for children.

he rst six years of a child's life are critical for brain

as the brain undergoes signi cant development that shape

in Mumbai and his mother busy managing a household of

The Critical Role of Early Childhood
During the rst six years, a child's brain is extraordinarily
plastic, meaning it is highly responsive to environmental
stimuli and experiences. This period sees the formation of
nearly a billion neurons, each serving as a building block
for the brain's complex network of connections. Activities
like cognitive movement, color perception, shape
recognition, and motor skill development are established

g

fi

fi

ff

fi

27

during this time, laying the groundwork for more complex
skills later in life.
The human brain is a remarkable organ, characterized by
its unparalleled capacity for adaptation. From the earliest
stages of life, the brain begins a complex process of
development, orchestrating a series of changes that lay the
foundation for cognitive, emotional, and social behaviors.
Understanding early childhood brain development is
crucial for fostering environments that support optimal
growth and for mitigating the e ects of adverse conditions
that can hinder a child's potential.
In the absence of formal daycare or early education
centers, Manu's early development was supported by the
care and attention of his older siblings. Their involvement
helped foster his cognitive and emotional growth, allowing
him to develop foundational skills that would later support
his adaptability and success in life. The natural
environment of Mandvi, with its open spaces and the
freedom to explore, also contributed to his early cognitive
and physical development.

Lessons from Early Childhood Development
Manu's experiences growing up in a large family, with
older siblings who acted as mentors and caregivers,
highlight the importance of a supportive environment in
early childhood. These early interactions helped shape his
ability to adapt, learn, and innovate—qualities that would
serve him well throughout his life. The involvement of his
siblings provided a rich, interactive environment that was

ff

28

crucial for solidifying the neural connections that underpin
cognitive and physical skills.
Manu's story underscores the importance of providing
children with a nurturing environment during their
formative years. The quality of time spent by parents and
caregivers in these early years can have lasting e ects on a
child's development, in uencing their ability to learn,
adapt, and succeed later in life. As Manu would later
re ect, these early experiences set the foundation for his
lifelong journey of learning and innovation, proving that
the right environment in early childhood can indeed lead to
miraculous results.

Implications for Modern ECD Practices
The lessons from Manu's early childhood are still relevant
today, particularly in the context of modern Early
Childhood Development (ECD) practices. The science of
ECD emphasizes the need for high-quality, interactive
experiences during the rst six years of life, when the brain
is most malleable. Engaging children in activities that
stimulate cognitive and physical growth, providing proper
nutrition, and ensuring a safe and nurturing environment
are all critical components of successful ECD.
Parents, caregivers, and educators can draw on these
lessons to create environments that support the holistic
development of children. By prioritizing early childhood
education and care, society can ensure that all children can
reach their full potential, laying the groundwork for a
healthier, more innovative, and adaptable future
generation.

Readers, as you re ect on your own childhood, try to
recall memories from your earliest years. Most of us have
little to no memory of our lives before the age of four, and
only eeting glimpses of experiences between the ages of
four and six. Yet, these formative years are when some of
the most crucial brain development occurs, laying the
foundation for the person you would become. Think about
the in uences, the environment, and the interactions that
shaped you during this time—how they may have
contributed to your cognitive and emotional growth.
Now, consider the children in your life who are in this
critical age range. The actions you take—or fail to take—
during these early years will have a profound and lasting
impact on their development. Actively engaging with them,
providing enriching experiences, and nurturing their
growing minds are not just responsibilities but
opportunities to set them on a path toward lifelong success.
Missing out on this crucial developmental period can lead
to challenges that are di cult, if not impossible, to
overcome later in life. The investment you make in a child's
early brain development is one that will yield signi cant
returns, not just for them but for society.

The Brain as the Ultimate Organ of Adaptation
The brain's primary function is to process information
and orchestrate behavioral responses that enable humans
to navigate their environments. It adapts continually,
integrating sensory input with past experiences to produce
behaviors that are sometimes awe-inspiring and, at other
times, destructive. This adaptability is rooted in the brain's

fi

ffi

fl

fl

fl

30

structural and functional plasticity, which is most
pronounced during early childhood.

Historical Context of Early Childhood Brain
Development
The understanding of early childhood brain development
has evolved signi cantly over the centuries. In ancient
times, philosophers like Aristotle and Plato debated the
origins of knowledge, with some believing that children
were born as blank slates ("tabula rasa") to be shaped
entirely by experience, while others argued for innate
abilities present from birth.
It wasn't until the 18th century that scienti c inquiry into
child development began to take shape. Jean-Jacques
Rousseau, in his seminal work Émile, emphasized the
importance of early childhood education and the natural
development of children, laying the groundwork for
modern educational theory.
In the 20th century, pioneers like Maria Montessori and
Jean Piaget advanced our understanding of how children
learn and develop. Montessori's educational approach,
rooted in the belief that children learn best through handson, self-directed activities, re ected a deep respect for the
child's natural developmental processes. Jean Piaget's
theory of cognitive development, which outlined how
c h i l d r e n c o n s t r u c t k n o w l e d ge t h r o u g h s t a ge s ,
revolutionized our understanding of the mental growth
that occurs during early childhood.

fi

fl

fi

31

The latter half of the 20th century saw the advent of
neuroscience, which began to uncover the biological
underpinnings of early brain development. The
groundbreaking work of scientists such as Dr. Benjamin
Spock and Dr. T. Berry Brazelton highlighted the critical
importance of the early years in shaping a child's future,
reinforcing the idea that the experiences children have
during this period can have lasting e ects on their brain
architecture and overall development.

Neuronal Growth and Early Connectivity
At birth, a child possesses nearly one billion neurons,
each serving as a potential building block for the brain's
complex network of connections. However, these neurons
are not yet fully interconnected. Over the rst few months
of life, the brain undergoes rapid synaptogenesis, where
neurons begin forming connections through synapses,
creating intricate pathways that link the brain to various
parts of the body.
These neural connec tions are critic al for the
development of physical and cognitive functions. For
example, a seemingly simple action such as turning the
head toward a light or sound source involves a complex
interplay of neural signals between the eyes, ears, neck
muscles, and the brain. Once an action is successfully
executed, the brain retains this connection, reinforcing the
neural pathway and making future similar actions more
e cient. This process of trial, error, and retention is
foundational for all future learning and development.

fi

ff

ffi

32

The Critical First Six Years
The rst six years of life are especially crucial for brain
development, as this period sees the most rapid and
signi cant growth in neural connections and cognitive
abilities. During this time, foundational activities such as
cognitive movement, color perception, shape recognition,
and motor skills development are established. These
activities are not isolated; they are deeply interconnected
with the synchronization of the body's physical parts,
including the eyes, ears, hands, feet, tongue, teeth, and
muscles.
As the brain and body work together to master basic
functions, these early years lay the groundwork for more
complex cognitive and physical skills that will be built upon
throughout life. This is why the quality of time spent by
parents and caregivers during early childhood is so critical.
Engaging children in rich, interactive experiences helps to
solidify these neural connections, leading to what can often
be described as miraculous results in a child's
development.

Early Childhood Chapter: The Role of DNA,
ECD, and Challenging Circumstances in
Leadership Development
The journey of leadership often begins long before one
assumes a formal title. It is shaped by a complex interplay
of genetic factors (DNA), early childhood development
(ECD), and the challenging circumstances that forge
resilience and adaptability. These elements combine to
create a foundation upon which future leaders build their
skills, perspectives, and values.

ff

fl

38

The Role of DNA
DNA provides the raw material for potential—intelligence,
temperament, and natural inclinations are all in uenced by
genetic inheritance. However, DNA is only part of the story.
It sets the stage but does not determine the entire play.
Leadership qualities like curiosity, persistence, and the
ability to empathize with others can be in uenced by
genetic predispositions, yet they must be nurtured and
developed through experiences and education.developed
through experiences and education.
Early Childhood Development (ECD)
The rst six years of life are critical in shaping a child's
cognitive, emotional, and social abilities. High-quality ECD,
which includes proper nutrition, stimulating environments,
and supportive relationships, can signi cantly in uence a
child's potential for leadership. For Manu Shah, growing up
in a small city like Mandvi with the support of his older
siblings and minimal formal daycare options, the informal
learning and constant engagement with family members
played a crucial role in his cognitive development. This
early foundation set the stage for his ability to adapt,
innovate, and lead e ectively later in life.
Challenging Circumstances
Leadership is often homed in the crucible of adversity.
Challenging circumstances push individuals beyond their
comfort zones, forcing them to develop problem-solving
skills, resilience, and the ability to navigate uncertainty. For

fl

fl

fl

fi

ff

fi

39

Manu, the challenges of growing up in a large family, with
the added complexity of his father's absence due to work in
Mumbai, meant that he had to quickly learn to be selfreliant and resourceful. These early experiences of
managing life's di culties without the immediate presence
of a parental gure instilled in him the resilience and
adaptability that would later de ne his leadership style at
MSI.
Context and Quotes
T h e i n te r p l ay o f D NA , E C D, a n d c h a l l e n g i n g
circumstances can be likened to the words of Warren
Bennis: "The most dangerous leadership myth is that
leaders are born—that there is a genetic factor to
leadership. This myth asserts that people simply
either have certain charismatic qualities or not. That's
nonsense; in fact, the opposite is true. Leaders are
made rather than born."
Maria Montessori: "The greatness of the human
personality begins at the hour of birth. From this almost
mystic a rmation there comes what may seem a strange
conclusion—that education must start from birth."
Dr. Benjamin Spock: "Trust yourself. You know more than
you think you do."
Jean Piaget: "The principal goal of education in the schools
should be creating men and women who are capable of
doing new things, not simply repeating what other
generations have done."

1.7
Story of Resilience and Grit
This chapter recounts Manu Shah's early life in India, shaped by
economic hardships, political instability, and a strong family
foundation. Growing up in Kutch during challenging times, Manu
witnessed resilience and determination from his mother and
grandmothers. The food crisis of the 1950s, aided by the PL 480
program, left a lasting impact on his childhood. Despite these
struggles, Manu's passion for science and education grew, with the
support of his family. Inspired by opportunities in America and
driven by the encouragement of his brother, Manu pursued his
dream of studying in the United States, ultimately enrolling at
Purdue University.

41

rowing up in Mandvi, Manu was surrounded by the
strength and resilience of the women in his family.
His mother, a petite yet formidable gure, embodied
optimism and perseverance. "No matter how tough times
are, better days are always
ahead," she would often
say. His grandmothers,
from both sides remained a
constant presence in his
early life further reinforced
these values. The in uence
of these strong women
would shape Manu's
outlook on life and instill in
him an unyielding
determination to succeed.

Economic Hardships and the PL 480 Program
The late 1950s in India were marked by severe economic
hardships. The country's food crisis left an indelible mark
on Manu's childhood. In 1958, India's wheat crop slumped
by 15%, and the rice harvest was down by 12%, causing
market prices to soar. This situation was dire, with
widespread hunger and long lines for food supplies.
The United States stepped in with the PL 480 program,
o cially known as the Agricultural Trade Development and
Assistance Act of 1954. This program aimed to provide food
aid to developing countries, including India. The PL 480
program brought coarse red wheat, initially meant for
livestock, to India's hungry population.

fi

fl

ffi

42

Manu vividly recalls the hours spent waiting in line for
this wheat, which became a staple in the Shah household.
"We were told it was meant for American pigs, but back
then, we didn’t have an option.” Manu would later re ect.
Despite the coarse texture and unfamiliar taste, the wheat
and other food supplies like powdered milk and vegetable
oil were lifelines for lower middle-class Indian families
during this period of scarcity. Rika had her share of waiting
in line at age10 11 in Matunga, a suburb of Mumbai.

Sparking a Passion for Science
In 1959, Manu's school received a scholarship of 2000
rupees to start a science club (pre-STEM). To put this into
perspective, 2000 rupees in the late 1950s would be
roughly equivalent to about $400 at that time, a scanty
amount for a school of 2000 students in a suburb of
Mumbai. Though only in the ninth grade, Manu was
determined to join. Manu built a working telegraph,
impressing his teacher and earning a place in the club as its
youngest member. This experience not only fueled his
passion for science but also ignited his dream of going to
America—a land that seemed full of possibilities.

The Importance of Education
Education was highly valued in the Shah family. Manu's
father, despite having limited formal education, learned
English while working in Mombasa and became pro cient.
Manu's siblings, particularly his second sister, played a
signi cant role in his early education. By the age of four,

fl

fi

-

fi

43

Manu could recite multiplication tables of up to 20, a skill
that set him apart from his peers. However, he often felt
small and undernourished compared to others, which
impacted his self-esteem. Till date he is one of the best to
work with numbers out of 3000+ employees in MSI except
his two sons – Raj & Rup.
Manu's commitment to education was further solidi ed
by his family's belief in its transformative power. "Education
was the only way out," Manu recalls. "We didn't have
money, but we had ambition and the drive to learn."

Adolescence and Political Instability
Adolescence brought its own set of challenges. India's
political and economic instability, exacerbated by the 1962
war with China and the 1965 war with Pakistan, made the
future seem uncertain. Nehru's socialist policies, aimed at
industrializing the nation and reducing poverty, often fell
short of their ambitious goals. The First Five-Year Plan,
launched in 1951, focused on agrarian reform and
industrialization, but its mixed results led to widespread
frustration.
The 1962 Sino-Indian War, which ended in a humiliating
defeat for India, further strained the nation's resources and
morale. "We were misled to believe that India was not in
such bad shape," Manu recalls. "It wasn't until much later
that we realized how badly we had lost to China." The
subsequent war with Pakistan in 1965, while not as
disastrous, also failed to yield a decisive victory, further
compounding the nation's woes.

fi

44

These circumstances made Manu realize that for a better
future, he needed to look beyond India's borders. Inspired
by the tales of opportunity and the grandeur of the Statue
of Liberty, Manu began seriously considering the possibility
of moving to America. His brother, a constant source of
support and guidance, encouraged him to apply to
universities in the United States. Despite the nancial
hurdles, Manu was determined to make this dream a
reality.

Dreaming of America
In 1965, Manu's dream of America was fueled by the
inspirational gure of President John F. Kennedy, whose
assassination in 1963 had deeply a ected many young
Indians. "President Kennedy was very popular among the
youth in India," Manu re ects. "His vision and charisma
made us believe in the possibility of a better future." The
image of the Statue of Liberty, the Empire State Building,
and the promise of endless opportunities drove Manu to
pursue higher education in the United States.
His eldest brother Yashwant, who had always been a
guiding force in his life, urged him to pursue higher
education in America. With nancial help from his brother
and a loan from his hostel donor, Manu came to the United
States of America. He got admission to the prestigious
Purdue University — a decision that would change his life.
He chose Purdue among other universities such as UC
Berkeley was in uenced by Purdue’s reputation for
excellence in engineering and its relatively low cost.

for its strong engineering programs, Purdue attracted
students from around the world. Life at Purdue in 1967 was

Purdue o ered an opportunity to immerse in advanced

A Wa r t i m e We d d i n g Beginning of a Lifelong

This chapter details the story of Manu and Rika Shah’s rapid
engagement and wedding during the turbulent time of the 1971 IndoPakistani War. Despite the chaos of war and blackouts in Mumbai,
their families arranged a simple wedding on December 12, 1971, with
about 150 guests. Just 45 days after the wedding, the couple moved
to America to start their new life. Over the next 52 years, Manu and
Rika built a life lled with love, challenges, and shared
accomplishments, with their bond rooted in mutual respect and
understanding.

ecember 1971
was
a

India. The country
was in the midst of
the Bangladesh
Liberation War, with

pouring into India
from East Pakistan
(now Bangladesh) and
an imminent war with West Pakistan. Amidst this national

tradition and necessity, re ecting characteristic of Indian
families.

The Arranged Meeting and Rapid Engagement
Manu, having recently graduated from the prestigious
VJTI College in Matunga, Mumbai, was looking for a life
partner. His family had known Rika’s family for a long time,
both coming from large middle-class backgrounds in the
Kutch region. Although they had never met, their families
were convinced that Manu and Rika were a perfect match.
Rika, living in the same suburb where Manu had studied,
was also looking for someone settled in the USA. Her family
wanted her to marry a man who could provide stability and
opportunity. Manu’s family, on the other hand, sought a
companion and partner for Manu who would also be a
nurturing mother to his future children.

fl

59

The families arranged for Manu and Rika to meet on

This brief courtship was typical of the time, especially in
arranged marriages, where family connections and mutual
respect were paramount.

Historical Context: The 1971 Indo-Pakistani
War and the Birth of Bangladesh
The 1971 Indo-Pakistani War was a major con ict that led
to the creation of Bangladesh. The roots of this war lay in
the political and social tensions between East Pakistan
(now Bangladesh) and West Pakistan (now Pakistan). East
Pakistan sought independence due to cultural, linguistic,
and political discrimination by the ruling West Pakistani
regime. The con ict escalated into a full-scale war in
December 1971 when India intervened in support of East
Pakistan after millions of refugees ed to India to escape
the brutal military crackdown by West Pakistani forces. The
war resulted in a decisive victory for India, leading to the
surrender of Pakistani forces in East Pakistan and the
establishment of Bangladesh as an independent nation on
December 16, 1971. This war not only reshaped the
geopolitical landscape of South Asia but also highlighted
the enduring struggle for self-determination and human
rights.

fi

The Wedding: A Simple A air in a Time of War

other better. The wedding
took place amidst the war
with Pakistan, which led
to blackouts in Mumbai
and a city on high alert.
Despite these challenging
circumstances, the
wedding went ahead as

Given the wartime situation, only about 150 people could
attend the wedding ceremony and reception. By 5 PM,
everyone had left, and the newlyweds were left to start
their journey together. Manu’s parents were happy, and
despite the simplicity of the ceremony, it marked the
beginning of a remarkable partnership.

Starting a New Life in America
Just 45 days after their wedding, Manu and Rika left for

A Lifetime of Companionship and Growth

Re ections and Lessons Learned
The story of Manu and Rika’s marriage is a testament to
the power of commitment and adaptability. Despite the

Their journey has been one of shared dreams, mutual

1.11
The Legacy of Shree
Gangjibhai Parekh - A Man
of Principle and Resilience
Shree Gangjibhai Parekh, Rika Shah's father, was a man of
resilience, strong principles, and unwavering dedication to his
family and community. Born in 1893 in Kutch Mundra, India,
Gangjibhai overcame early life hardships, including losing his
parents and surviving the devastating plague. After moving to
Mumbai for work, he became a trusted gure in his business and
was known for his generosity, community service, and strong Jain
faith. He was deeply respected for his meticulous nature, negotiating
skills, and commitment to providing his children with a good
education. His legacy of integrity and compassion continues to
inspire his descendants.

fi

67

ika Shah’s
f a t h e r, S h re e
Gangjibhai Parekh, was
a man whose life
e x e m p l i
e d

despite numerous
adversities. Born in 1893
in Kutch Mundra, India,
Gangjibhai faced

Orphaned early in life, he grew up amid the devastating
plague that swept through India between 1896 and 1921,
claiming millions of lives. Despite losing many relatives and
friends to the disease, Gangjibhai survived and would go on
to live a life lled with wisdom, integrity, and unwavering
dedication to his family and community.
In 1929, Gangjibhai married Chanduben, who had also lost
her parents at a young age. Together, they built a family
and a life in Kutch Mundra, where their rst daughter,
Dahiben, was born in 1932. Soon after, Gangjibhai
employer, Kalyanji Dhanji & Co., transferred him to their
new o ce in Bombay (now Mumbai). Tasked with growing
the business in this bustling metropolis, Gangjibhai worked
diligently, proving himself to be not just a capable
businessman but a trustworthy and reliable asset to his

fi

fi

fi

ffi

68

company. His employers placed complete trust in him,
never questioning his work or decisions.
In 1939, Gangjibhai moved his family to Matunga, a suburb
of Bombay, where they would grow to include four sons
and four daughters. Known a ectionately as “Bhai” by his
children, he was a man of great principle. His attire
remained constant throughout his life—he wore a
traditional jabho with a long jacket, dhoti, and black topi
(hat), and in his later years, carried an umbrella, which he
used for support instead of a cane.
Gangjibhai was a man deeply connected to his community.
He believed in sharing and giving back, especially when it
came to food. Every morning, he would feed the street
dogs with rotla and o er grains to pigeons, believing that
caring for animals was a noble and necessary act. His
meticulous nature extended to every aspect of his life,
especially food. He personally inspected raw materials and
ensured that everything purchased for the home was of the
highest quality. His focus on pure, clean, and healthy food
earned him great respect in the community. When food
was shared by him, it was known to be perfect in weight,
price, and quality, and he often asked family members to
distribute it at cost price to others.
One of Gangjibhai’s most enduring traits was his
exceptional negotiating ability. He became known for his
famous tactic of intentionally leaving his umbrella behind
when a negotiation was not going well. This clever strate y
allowed him to return to the client’s o ce under the
pretense of retrieving his umbrella and restart negotiations
with fresh ener y, often leading to a successful outcome.

g

ff

ff

g

His children would later recall this lesson as a profound
business strate y—always keep the door open for a second

Gangjibhai’ s commitment to his Jain faith was equally
remarkable. He strictly followed the practice of Choviyar,
refraining from eating after sunset. If he arrived home late
from work and missed sunset, he would skip dinner
altogether, a testament to his discipline and devotion. His
belief in living a simple and disciplined life extended to his
interactions with others, earning him a reputation for being
wise and thoughtful. Many in the community sought his
advice, and despite having a limited budget, Gangjibhai
ensured that all his children received a good education,
something he believed was critical to their success.
Shree Gangjibhai Parekh’s legacy is one of resilience,
wisdom, and profound integrity. He was a man who not
only overcame the adversities of his early life but used
those experiences to shape his character and guide his
family with strong moral values. His principles of trust,
fairness, and discipline left an indelible mark on those
around him and continue to in uence the lives of his
descendants. His life stands as a testament to the power of
living with purpose, integrity, and compassion, and his
story serves as an enduring inspiration to his family and
community.

1.12
Sheth to Shah & Parekh
DNA
This chapter delves into the rich history of the Sheth, Shah, and
Parekh surnames, exploring their deep roots in India’s mercantile
and trading traditions. The name "Shah" is tied to business
leadership, especially in Jain and Vaishya communities, while
"Sheth" historically symbolized wealth and social prominence. The
Parekh surname is associated with expertise in precious metals.
Each name re ects a legacy of ethical business practices,
community leadership, and philanthropy.

fl

71

Shah: Origins, Evolution, and In uence
The surname Shah is one of the most recognizable names
in the Indian subcontinent, especially within business and
nance sectors. The word originates from the Persian
"Shah," which historically referred to a king or emperor.
However, in the Indian context, the title evolved to signify
leadership in the business world, especially among the Jain
and Vaishya communities
1. Historical Context
• Origins in Persia: The word Shah came into India
during the rule of Persian and Mughal empires. While
Shah was originally a title for royalty and rulers, over
time, it was adopted by in uential traders and
merchants, particularly those of Jain and Hindu
communities, especially in Gujarat, Rajasthan, and
Maharashtra.
• Merchant Class: The adoption of Shah by Jain and
Vaishya families represented leadership in trade and
commerce. Gujarat, known for its vibrant trading culture,
became a hub for merchant communities, and many
successful traders adopted the title as a mark of their

fl

as their association with various social and religious
communities.

economic power and prestige.
• Economic Leadership: Shahs were known for their
role as nancial leaders in local economies, often acting
as bankers, nanciers, and large-scale traders. The
surname symbolized success, ethics, and responsibility
in business dealings, and it became synonymous with
trust and respect within business circles.
2. Association with Jainism
• Jain Ethos of Trade: Jainism’s principles of nonviolence (ahimsa) and truth (satya) played a crucial role
in shaping the moral compass of the Shah families. This
ethical foundation helped them build business empires
that were known not just for their wealth, but for their
integrity and philanthropy.
• Philanthropy and Social Responsibility: Shahs are
often associated with large donations to religious and
educational causes. Jain businessmen like Virchand
Gandhi, a prominent Jain scholar, and other in uential
Shahs contributed greatly to the development of
charitable institutions, temples, and educational
establishments in India and abroad.
3. Modern In uence
• Diaspora: As India opened up to global trade, many
Shah families expanded their businesses to international
markets, particularly East Africa, the UK, and the USA.
Shah communities now ourish in countries with

The Sheth Surname: Historical Signi cance
and Evolution
The surname Sheth (sometimes spelled as Seth, Sethia,
or Seth) has deep historical roots in India, particularly
within the trading and merchant communities of Gujarat,
Rajasthan, and other northern parts of India. The term
Sheth historically signi ed a person of great wealth,
property, and in uence, often a landowner, banker, or
merchant. It carried an air of prestige, connoting not just
nancial success but also social prominence and leadership
within the community.
1. Meaning and Origins
• Historical Role: In its most traditional sense, the word
Sheth is derived from the Sanskrit "Shreshta," meaning
excellent or eminent. In this context, a Sheth was
considered the head of a large mercantile establishment,
usually a person with signi cant property holdings and
in uence in commerce. Historically, Sheths were often
nanciers or bankers who controlled large sums of
money and owned substantial assets.

2. Social Status
• Symbol of Wealth and Power: The Sheth surname
was associated with power, in uence, and wealth. Those

upper echelons of society. In many cases, the Sheth
family would be responsible for supporting temples,
schools, and charities, further solidifying their standing
as pillars of the community.
• Prestige and Exclusivity: Given the connotations of
great wealth and property ownership, the Sheth surname
became synonymous with an elite class of people. It
conveyed a sense of exclusivity and entitlement,
signaling that those with the Sheth surname were among
the most a uent in society.
3. Change from Sheth to Shah
• Shedding the Elite Identit y: Manu's great

Conclusion: The Legacy of Sheth and Shah
The decision to change the family surname from Sheth to
Shah represented more than just a simple name change; it
signi ed a shift in identity, values, and social outlook.
While the Sheth surname was historically associated with
great wealth, power, and exclusivity, the Shah name
allowed the family to embrace a more modest, yet equally
respected, professional identity.
By adopting the Shah name, Manu's great grandfather
aligned the family with the hardworking, ethical, and
intellectually driven communities of traders, accountants,
and professionals. This change likely contributed to the
family’s success in business, including their legacy in trade,
commerce, and nance, which continues today.
The journey from Sheth to Shah illustrates how names
carry not only personal history but also social, cultural, and
professional signi cance, and how adapting to changing
times can help ensure long-term success and relevance in a
shifting world.

Parekh: Assayers, Merchants, and Cultural
Custodians

history, particularly connected to the trade of precious
metals and money lending. The word "Parekh" comes from
the Sanskrit "Pariksha," which means examiner, re ecting

1. Historical Context
• Goldsmiths and Assayers: The Parekh surname is

the purity of metals. This work required a high level of skill,
trustworthiness, and integrity, as the results directly impacted
the value of trade goods.
• Guilds and Merchant Associations: The Parekh families
were often part of merchant guilds, where they were entrusted
with responsibilities that required a reputation for fairness and
precision. Their knowledge of metals, gems, and nance made
them key gures in local and international trade, particularly
in Gujarat and Rajasthan.
2. Role in Jain and Vaishya Communities

charity were re ected in their business practices. Many Parekh
families were not only successful in trade but also in social

educational institutions.
• Vaishya In uence: In Hindu society, the Parekhs were part
of the Vaishya caste, traditionally responsible for trade and
commerce. This caste distinction reinforced their role in the
economic systems of ancient and medieval India, particularly
in cities like Surat, Ahmedabad, and other trade centers of
Gujarat.

1.15
Parenting – Raising Raj and
Rup in America
This chapter explores how Rika and Manu Shah navigated the
challenges of raising their sons, Raj and Rup, in Fort Wayne,
Indiana, while running a business as Indian immigrants. They
emphasized family values, the importance of public schooling, and
involvement in the family business to teach responsibility. Their
parenting philosophy was built on leading by example, fostering
independence, and promoting emotional wellbeing through nontraditional activities like camping and family debates. The Midwest’s
strong work ethic and sense of community shaped their approach to
life and business, passing these values on to their children.

91

any people have asked Rika and Manu about their
parenting journey—how they managed to raise
two boys, Raj and Rup, in the middle of America while
running a business, and how they navigated the challenges
of being a small family of Indian immigrants in a
predominantly white community. This chapter dives into
their approach to parenting, the values they instilled, and
the lessons they learned while raising their children in a
unique environment.

Raising Kids in a New Culture
Rika and Manu raised their children in Fort Wayne,
Indiana, a place where they were surrounded by families
who were mostly white and where cultural diversity was
not the norm. Yet, they believed that the strength of their
own family values and the support of their small, close-knit
family would provide Raj and Rup with the foundation they
needed to thrive. From an early age, Raj and Rup were sent
to daycare at a local church, followed by attending a public
school. While many well-to-do and educated parents in
their community were sending their children to private
schools, Rika and Manu felt con dent that the public school
system would be just as valuable for their children,
believing that academic excellence comes from within the
child, not the school alone; Kids should learn and work
with all kinds of background not just elites.
They faced the challenge of juggling parenting while
building their edgling export business. Manu often
traveled extensively for his job at International Truck and
later for MSI, while Rika managed the house, kids, and the

fi

fl

92

business startup. There were no internet or cell phones in
those days, so the family relied on clever solutions, like
using an 800 number for MSI to ensure Manu could stay
connected to the business and the kids while traveling.
Despite the challenges, they made it work, ensuring that
the family and business ourished side by side..

Involving Kids in Business
From a young age, Raj and
Rup were introduced to the
family business. Simple

Cerritos, California, setting the stage for a new chapter in
both the business and their lives.

Parenting Philosophy
Rika and Manu embraced a parenting philosophy rooted
in their own experiences and values, always guided by their
belief in the importance of DNA and the example set by
parents. They believed strongly that children do what they

fl

93

see, not what they are told. Setting a positive example through their hard work, integrity, and devotion to family—
was paramount. The idea that “children learn by watching
and listening” shaped the way they parented, fostering an
environment where curiosity, innovation, and open
communication were encouraged.
Importantly, Rika and Manu never pushed perfectionism
or placed undue pressure on their children to perform.
They encouraged individuality, never comparing Raj or Rup
to each other or to other children. Instead, they focused on
helping wherever weaknesses emerged, building strengths
with patience and support.

E mo t i o n a l Ne e d s a n d No n -Tra d i t i o n a l
Activities
Recognizing the importance of emotional wellbeing, they
made sure to address Raj and Rup's emotional needs,
encouraging debates from an early age, respecting their
views even if they changed with time, and nurturing
inquisitiveness. Family time was not just limited to business
—camping trips, going to games, and engaging in
philanthropic work during Thanksgiving and Christmas
were important non-traditional activities that brought the
family together.

Financial Lessons and Curiosity
Rika and Manu also believed in teaching nancial
responsibility early on. They opened bank accounts for
their children within days of their birth, adding cash gifts to

fi

94

the accounts and teaching Raj and Rup the value of money.
More importantly, they nurtured curiosity, innovation, and
outdoor activities. The local library became a favorite
destination, books were abundant, and the kids were
always encouraged to ask questions, experiment, and
explore.

Counter will Instinct and Encouraging
Independence
A unique part of their philosophy was recognizing and
respecting the “counter-will instinct”—the natural tendency
of children to do the opposite of what they are told. Rather
than discouraging this instinct, they used it as a tool for
learning, fostering curiosity and the desire to forge their
own path. They saw this as an important part of developing
independence and resilience.
Through their unique approach to parenting, Rika and
Manu balanced family, business, and the cultural
challenges of raising children in America, ensuring that Raj
and Rup grew into responsible, curious, and independent
adults. Their parenting style was based on love, respect,
and the belief that children will ourish if given the right
foundation, the freedom to explore, and the support to
grow.

Embracing American Values in the Midwest
(1972 1984)
From the moment Manu and Rika Shah arrived in
America, they were struck by the abundance of

The Midwest: A Land of Opportunity and
Community
Living in Fort Wayne, Indiana, from 1973 to 1984, Manu
and Rika were surrounded by hardworking, middle-class
families who prioritized family, education, and community.
They observed that, unlike in many other parts of the
world, opportunities in America were plentiful and
accessible to those willing to work hard. This realization
reinforced their belief in the American Dream and fueled
their determination to succeed both personally and
professionally.

Rejecting Negative In uences
While the Midwest o ered a wealth of positive in uences,
Manu and Rika were also acutely aware of the potential
pitfalls that could derail their family's progress. They made
a conscious decision to avoid negative in uences such as
drugs, gangs, alcohol, smoking, partying, and gambling.
They had not come to America for these activities, and they
were determined to shield their family from them. Instead,
they focused on the values that had brought them to the
United States: hard work, education, and the opportunity
to build a better life.
In this regard, they were successful in instilling these
values in their children. Even today, Raj and Rup are proud
of their Midwest roots, grateful for the solid foundation
their parents provided. They often speak about how
growing up in the Midwest, surrounded by educated,
hardworking people, shaped their outlook on life and their
approach to business and family.

Simple Parenting Rules: Empowering Children
for Their Own Future
In their journey as parents, Manu and Rika followed a set
of guiding principles that helped them raise their children,
Raj and Rup, with a focus on growth, independence, and
positivity. Here are a few simple but e ective rules that they
embraced:
1. Let Kids Chart Their Own Path
Every child must have the freedom to build their own
future and achieve their own successes. As parents, it's
important to assist them when needed, but not to
overpressure them. If your child doesn’t enjoy activities like
dancing, robotics, or music, it's essential to respect their
preferences and not force them into something that doesn't
resonate with them.

ff

fi

99

Children should never feel pressured or compared to
others. Whether it's regarding family circumstances,
nancial situations, or even the history of relatives,
negative feelings should be avoided. It's crucial to create an
environment where they feel supported rather than
burdened by expectations they cannot control.
3. Encourage Growth, No Matter How Big or Small
Growth should be encouraged in every aspect of a child’s
life, whether in academics, sports, or hobbies. Being
number one is not the goal. It’s more important that
children learn, improve, and enjoy the process, even if they
don’t achieve the highest scores or ranks in school or
games. Failure should never be viewed as the end, but as a
learning experience.
4. Focus on Positive Stories
Whenever possible, share positive stories that inspire
and uplift children. Focus on their strengths and the good
things that happen, no matter how small. Positivity is a key
ingredient in nurturing self-con dence and resilience in
children.
5. Teach Contentment and Acceptance
One of the most important lessons is to accept the
tools, assets, and resources we have and to work with them
to the best of our ability. Children should be discouraged
from the "if only" mindset—"if we had more, we could have
100
fi

fi

2. Avoid Negative Comparisons or Pressure

done better." Teach them the value of contentment and the
belief that they can achieve great things with the resources
available to them.
By following these simple rules, Manu and Rika ensured
that their children grew up feeling empowered, supported,
and encouraged, while allowing them the freedom to
pursue their own paths and dreams. This parenting
approach created a foundation of positivity, resilience, and
self-reliance that Raj and Rup carry with them to this day.

principles Manu and Rika followed:

2.1
The Entrepreneurial Journey
of MSI
This chapter explores how Manu and Rika Shah built MSI from a
small home-based business into a global leader in the surfacing
industry. Manu’s entrepreneurial journey began out of necessity,
and his belief that entrepreneurship cannot be taught but is driven
by circumstance and innovation. Rika played an equally important
role, bringing simplicity and balance to business decisions.
Together, they took calculated risks, including securing a contract
for the Vietnam War Memorial, which propelled MSI into the
spotlight. Their approach to entrepreneurship is centered around
continuous learning, adaptability, and fostering a culture of
innovation at MSI.

110

ntrepreneurship is often
envisioned as a journey,
not just a destination—a
concept that Manu deeply
resonates with. He and his wife
Rika's entrepreneurial spirit
has been central to MSI's
growth from a small homebased operation to a global
leader in the surfacing
industry. We will explore key

Manu and Rika, re ecting on their personal experiences,
the growth of MSI, and the broader impacts of their
entrepreneurial vision.

The Essence of Entrepreneurship
Manu often re ects on the essence of entrepreneurship,
challenging the notion that it can be taught. "Many colleges
try to teach entrepreneurship, but I'm not sure you can
teach it. Either you're born an entrepreneur or
circumstances make you one, although, the basics can be
taught through practical experiences, college course,
internships and mentorship programs." he states
emphatically. Manu believes that necessity is the true
mother of invention. "If someone puts you on an island
alone, you either die or nd a way to survive. That’s how
entrepreneurship works—it's about doing what you
wouldn't in a comfortable environment."

Manu's Path to Entrepreneurship:
Manu never set out to become an entrepreneur in the
traditional sense. In fact, he didn’t even know what the
term meant until 2007, when he was awarded the Ernst &
Young National Entrepreneur of the Year award. By then,
he had already built a ourishing business and garnered
national recognition, yet his journey into entrepreneurship
was more a natural progression than a deliberate pursuit.
For Manu, entrepreneurship was less about titles and more
about curiosity, problem-solving, and the drive to innovate.
It was something that had always been part of his life, even
from childhood.
From a young age, Manu’s inquisitiveness shaped his
approach to life. Growing up in a small apartment in India,
he found creative ways to optimize the limited space. This
curiosity extended to other aspects of his life—whether it
was organizing trips with fellow teenagers using detailed
maps typically reserved for foreign travelers or nding new
ways to navigate the challenges of daily life. Manu's
inventive spirit also came into play when, as a teenager, he
helped coordinate activities and solve logistical problems
that others often overlooked.
Manu's journey to the United States for further education
was yet another testament to his determination. Faced with
limited nancial resources and the challenge of learning
English, he secured loans to fund his studies at Purdue
University. His resilience and foresight in preparing for jobs
while still struggling with language barriers re ected his
ability to innovate under pressure. This same spirit later
drove Manu to launch a business with his wife Rika, even as

For Manu, entrepreneurship was never about chasing

challenges, and continuously pushing boundaries. He
believes that entrepreneurship isn’t con ned to the realm
of business; rather, it’s a mindset that can be applied to
every aspect of life. Whether it's solving logistical issues,
optimizing resources, or nding new ways to overcome
obstacles, Manu’s entrepreneurial spirit continues to guide
him. "Entrepreneurship is everywhere and should be in
your life—whether or not someone calls you an
entrepreneur," Manu says.
This perspective is grounded in his own journey. Manu's

Historical Context
•
Post-Colonial India's Economic Landscape
(1950s-1970s): Manu’s journey from India to the U.S. in the 1970s
re ects a period when India was transitioning from colonial rule to
building its own economy. The country’s focus was largely on selfreliance, and opportunities for entrepreneurship were limited due to
stringent economic policies. For individuals like Manu, leaving
India to seek educational and business opportunities abroad was
not only a personal choice but also a necessity shaped by broader
economic forces.
•
Immigration Waves and Economic Contributions
(1960s-1980s): The Shah family’s entrepreneurial venture
coincided with signi cant waves of Indian immigration to the U.S.,
driven by changes in U.S. immigration law in 1965 that favored
skilled workers. The contribution of immigrant entrepreneurs like
Manu to the American economy was profound, particularly in
sectors like technolo y and small business, where they brought new
ideas and international perspectives.
•
Globalization and Shifts in Trade (1980s-1990s): MSI's
pivot to natural stone products during the early 1980s capitalized
on emerging globalization trends, which were transforming
industries worldwide. As global supply chains became more
integrated, MSI’s ability to source materials from places like India
and its eventual role in major projects. This period also saw shifts in
U.S. manufacturing, where imports became a key component of
business strate y.
