4.7
War and Peace - Manu’s
Learning in Life
The Complex Relationship Between Destruction
and Reconstruction in the Context of War and
History
Manu Shah’s life and leadership philosophy are deeply rooted in
values of non-violence, integrity, and ethical confrontation, shaped
by his Jain upbringing and personal experiences with childhood
bullies. He learned early the importance of standing up against
wrongdoing, a principle he applied throughout his life and business.
Manu's approach to both personal and professional con icts
emphasizes resolving issues swiftly and fairly, avoiding destructive
competition, and fostering long-term trust. This commitment to
integrity helped build MSI into a company with strong ethical
practices and a culture of mutual respect.

fl

709

anu and Rika Shah, both born into Jain families,
have deeply embedded values of non-violence
(Ahimsa) and the pursuit of peaceful solutions. Jainism, an
ancient religion, emphasizes the sanctity of all life forms
and the importance of living in harmony. As a student of
history, Manu has always been intrigued by the paradox of
how signi cant progress often emerges from the aftermath
of destruction and war. Manu’s struggle is depicted here
into the intricate relationship between destruction,
reconstruction, and peace, and the lessons that can be
drawn from history.

Arguments for the Necessity of Destruction
1. Elimination of Threat
Sometimes, the destruction of military infrastructure,
oppressive regimes, or sources of con ict is necessary to
eliminate immediate threats and create conditions for
lasting peace. Historical examples include the dismantling
of totalitarian regimes that posed signi cant threats to
global security.
2. Catalyst for Change
Major con icts can expose deep-rooted societal issues
and injustices, acting as catalysts for change and reform.
For instance, the civil rights movements in various
countries often gained momentum following periods of
con ict and upheaval.
3. Uni cation
Shared experiences of hardship and loss during
wartime can sometimes lead to a sense of unity and

fi

fl

fl

fi

fi

fl

710

common purpose among a population. This unity can pave
the way for reconciliation and cooperation in the
aftermath, as seen in the reconstruction of Europe postWorld War II.

Arguments Against the Necessity of
Destruction
1. Humanitarian Cost
The destruction caused by war in icts immense
su ering and loss of life on civilian populations. The most
vulnerable members of society disproportionately bear this
cost. The humanitarian crises resulting from wars are often
profound and long-lasting.
2. Cycle of Violence
Destruction can perpetuate cycles of hatred and
violence, making long-term peace more di cult to achieve.
Trauma and resentment can linger for generations, fueling
future con icts. The Middle East con icts provide stark
examples of how destruction can lead to prolonged cycles
of violence.
3. Unintended Consequences
Wa r c a n h a v e u n f o r e s e e n a n d u n i n t e n d e d
consequences, destabilizing entire regions and creating
new con icts. The destruction of infrastructure and
institutions can set back development and progress by
decades, as seen in the prolonged instability in regions like
Afghanistan and Iraq.

ffi

fl

fl

fl

fl

ff

711

The Path to Reconstruction and Peace
1. Rebuilding with Justice and Equity
- The destruction caused by war can create
opportunities to rebuild societies in more just and
equitable ways. Post-war reconstruction e orts should
focus on addressing the root causes of con ict and
promoting social justice.
2. Promoting Reconciliation and Healing
- E orts to foster reconciliation and healing are crucial
for breaking cycles of violence. Truth and reconciliation
commissions, such as those in South Africa, have played
vital roles in addressing past injustices and promoting
national healing.
3. Investing in Humanitarian and Development Aid
- Providing humanitarian and development aid to wartorn regions can help rebuild infrastructure, support
displaced populations, and promote economic recovery.
International cooperation and support are essential for
successful reconstruction e orts.

Conclusion: Weighing the Costs and Bene ts
The relationship between destruction and reconstruction
or peace is not always linear or predictable. While
destruction can sometimes lead to positive change, it is not
a guaranteed or desirable outcome. The costs of war are
immense, and the path to peace and reconstruction is often
long and arduous.

fi

fl

ff

ff

ff

712

Ultimately, whether destruction is deemed "necessary"
depends on the speci c context, the goals of the con ict,
and the values and perspectives of those involved. It is
crucial to weigh the potential bene ts of destruction
against its enormous costs and to explore alternative paths
toward peace and reconciliation whenever possible.

Manu's Lesson: Confronting Evil When

The Childhood Lessons
Manu's life has been marked by moments of profound
learning, often stemming from personal confrontations
with moral and ethical dilemmas. One of the most
signi cant lessons Manu learned and occasionally applied
throughout his life was, "There comes a time when evil or
evilness must be destroyed." This lesson was rooted in a
couple of formative incidents during his childhood.
At the age of nine, Manu encountered a challenging
situation involving a neighborhood teenager, a potential
hoodlum. This older boy convinced Manu to steal from his
oldest brother’s stamp collection. Manu did so twice before
realizing the immorality of his actions. When he attempted
to stop, the hoodlum resorted to blackmail, threatening to
report Manu to his family if he didn't continue stealing
more valuable stamps. After two sleepless nights lled with
anxiety and fear, Manu mustered the courage to confront
the teen hoodlum, telling him he was no longer afraid and
would no longer comply. This act of bravery ended the
blackmail, and when Manu reported the entire ordeal to his
older brother, he received praise and a blessing for his
integrity and courage.
Another de ning incident occurred when Manu was 14.
In a community of about 30 teenage boys, another local
hoodlum began to dominate and terrorize the kids. This
went on for months until Manu, the smallest among the

fi

fi

fi

714

children, formed a group of six boys. They decided to take
a stand and physically attacked and confronted the bully.
Their courage and uni ed action scared the hoodlum so
much that he never bothered the neighborhood kids again.
These experiences taught Manu valuable lessons about
standing up against injustice, power of working in a group
and dealing with bullies e ectively.
"The only thing necessary for the triumph of evil is
for good men to do nothing." - Edmund Burke This quote
captures the essence of Manu's actions as a child when he
stood up against the neighborhood bully and the hoodlum,
demonstrating that taking a stand is crucial in overcoming
evil.
"Courage is resistance to fear, mastery of fear – not
absence of fear." - Mark Twain Manu's bravery in
confronting the hoodlum and the bully despite his fears
exempli es this sentiment.

Applying the Lessons in Adult Life and
Business
These childhood lessons signi cantly shaped Manu’s
approach to life and business at MSI. The principles of
confronting and addressing wrongdoing were applied to
various aspects of his professional journey. Whether
dealing with dominating and unreasonable customers,
crooked and cheap suppliers, or employees and relatives
who attempted to exploit emotional relationships for
personal gain, Manu knew when to stand rm and take
decisive action.

when faced with suppliers who were dishonest or

Building a Culture of Integrity at MSI

This approach also extended to how Manu dealt with

The Concept of Mutually Assured Destruction
Manu was born in June 1945, often referred to as a "peace
baby," as his birth coincided with the end of World War II
and the dawn of a new era marked by the concept of
Mutually Assured Destruction (MAD). This principle, which
prevented large-scale con icts by ensuring that any
aggressor would face equal or greater destruction, has kept
major wars at bay since 1945. However, smaller, endless
wars such as the Korean War, Vietnam War, Afghan War,
and now the con ict in Ukraine have shown that while
MAD prevents total war, it does not guarantee peace.
The concept of MAD extends beyond geopolitics into the
business world. Manu applied this understanding to his
business strate y, recognizing that destructive competition

fl

ff

fl

ff

fl

g

fl

ffi

719

—such as undercutting prices meaninglessly, stealing
employees or patents, or sabotaging supply chains—leads to
mutual harm. Just as nations must nd ways to coexist and
compete without triggering catastrophic con ict,
businesses must navigate competition without engaging in
mutually destructive practices.
"An eye for an eye will only make the whole world
blind." - Mahatma Gandhi This quote is a reminder of the
destructive nature of retaliatory actions, relevant to both
geopolitics and business practices.
"The best way to predict the future is to create it." Peter Drucker By focusing on ethical competition and
long-term strategies, Manu aimed to shape a positive future
for MSI.

Practical Applications in Business
Manu’s philosophy was to compete with integrity and
focus on building long-term relationships rather than shortterm gains. For example, rather than engaging in price
wars that could hurt both MSI and its competitors, Manu
focused on di erentiating MSI through quality, customer
service, and innovation. This approach not only protected
MSI's market position but also fostered a more stable and
cooperative industry environment.
Similarly, Manu emphasized the importance of
respecting intellectual property and avoiding practices that
could lead to legal disputes or damage MSI's reputation. By
fostering a culture of innovation and ethical behavior, MSI

fl

fi

ff

720

could compete e ectively without resorting to destructive
tactics.
"In business, the competition will bite you if you
keep running; if you stand still, they will swallow
you." - Victor Kiam This quote re ects the importance of
continuous improvement and ethical competition in
business.
"The price of greatness is responsibility." - Winston
Churchill Manu’s approach to avoiding destructive
competition and fostering positive industry relationships is
encapsulated in this quote.

Personal and Community Relationships
The principle of avoiding mutually assured destruction
also applied to Manu’s personal life and interactions with
neighbors and relatives. He understood that con icts, if not
managed properly, could lead to lasting damage and
disrupt harmony. Manu’s approach was to seek peaceful
resolutions, foster mutual respect, and maintain strong,
positive relationships within his community and extended
family.
"Peace begins with a smile." - Mother Teresa This

4.8
Health, Near-Death
Experiences, and Lessons
Learned
Manu's life changed after a heart attack in 1999, leading to a
realization about the importance of health and work-life balance.
The near-death experience prompted him to adopt healthier habits
and rethink how MSI could thrive without his constant involvement.
By delegating responsibilities, focusing on succession planning, and
investing in employees and technolo y, Manu built a resilient
organization. His re ections on mortality deepened his commitment
to philanthropy and leaving a legacy that would bene t future
generations.

fi

g

fl

723

anu’s relentless drive and work ethic came at a
cost. In December 1999, during a party, he
experienced chest pain that led to a life-changing
revelation. "I had a chest pain, and my doctor, who was at
the party, advised me to visit the hospital if it got worse,"
Manu recalls. The next day, tests revealed nothing, but his
doctor suspected an issue and scheduled an angioplasty for
the following Tuesday. "Monday night, I had a heart attack,"
Manu says, marking the beginning of a signi cant chapter
in his life.

The First Heart Attack
The heart attack was a turning point. "In the ambulance,
I kept saying to myself, 'I don't want to die,'" Manu
remembers. His thoughts were not just about his family but
also about the thousands of employees depending on MSI.
"What would happen to the 3,000 people we support if
something happened to me?" he pondered. This experience
underscored the responsibility he felt towards his
employees and the broader MSI community.
The severity of his condition led to immediate medical
intervention. Manu underwent a bypass surgery in
February 2000, where ve arteries were bypassed or in
medical terms “quintuple bypass was conducted. However,
in April, he experienced another heart attack. "Four out of
the ve bypasses had failed," Manu recounts. This led to the
placement of multiple stents, a procedure that was
repeated several times over the years. "I now have eight
stents in my body, with six in the same artery," he explains.

fi

fi

fi

724

Lifestyle Changes and Lessons Learned
This near-death experience prompted Manu to
reevaluate his lifestyle. "I realized I had ignored my health
for too long," he admits. Despite his initial reluctance, he
began to incorporate regular exercise and a healthier diet
into his routine. "Exercise not only helps physically but also
releases endorphins that reduce stress," he notes. This
holistic approach to health became an integral part of his
daily life.
Manu also recognized the importance of mental health.
"The stress of managing multiple projects and helping
relatives added to my health issues," he says. Learning to
manage stress became a crucial part of his recovery
process. "Finding a balance between work and personal life
was essential," Manu explains. He credits his wife, Rika, for
her support and encouragement during this challenging
period.

The Broader Perspective
This period of health challenges also gave Manu a
broader perspective on life and business. "I realized the
importance of building a resilient organization that could
thrive even in my absence," he states. This led to a renewed
focus on succession planning and empowering his sons, Raj
and Rup, to take on leadership roles within MSI.
Manu's re ections on mortality have profoundly
in uenced his approach to life and work. "Knowing that life
is fragile makes you appreciate each moment more," he

fl

fl

725

re ects. This awareness has deepened his commitment to
philanthropy and his desire to make a lasting impact. "I
want to ensure that everything I do contributes to a better
world," Manu concludes.

Re ections
The late 1990s and early 2000s were a transformative
period for the healthcare industry, marked by signi cant
advancements in medical technolo y and treatments. The
development of stents, for example, revolutionized the
treatment of coronary artery disease, allowing for less
invasive procedures compared to traditional bypass
surgeries. Manu's multiple stent placements are a testament
to these medical advancements, which have saved
countless lives around the world.
The emphasis on lifestyle changes, particularly the
importance of exercise and stress management, re ects
broader societal shifts towards preventive healthcare. In
the 1990s, the rise of tness culture and increased
awareness of mental health marked a turning point in how
people approached their well-being. Manu's journey
mirrors this cultural shift, highlighting the importance of a
balanced lifestyle in achieving long-term health and
success.
This period also aligns with the broader movement
towards recognizing the importance of mental health.
In uential gures like Arianna Hu ngton, co-founder of

success beyond money and power to include well-being,

Building a Resilient Organization

The concept of resilience in business is critical, as noted

Investing in People and Technolo y

5.1
Global Impact
Manu and Rika Shah’s remarkable journey from India to building
MSI, a global enterprise committed to job creation and community
empowerment. Their early successes in the granite business laid the
foundation for supporting over 400,000 jobs across 35 countries by
2023, signi cantly impacting rural economies. Through the
Sarvamangal Family Trust and the Shah Happiness Foundation,
their philanthropic e orts focus on education, skill development,
and health initiatives, bene ting millions globally. Their enduring
legacy is one of empowering communities and making a lasting,
positive impact on the world.

fi

ff

fi

731

anu Shah’s journey from India to America in 1967
was marked by a deep-seated desire to create
opportunities for others, inspired by his own experiences.
Upon graduating from VJTI, a top engineering school in
India, Manu faced a challenging job market, despite his
credentials. This experience ignited a lifelong ambition to
not only succeed personally but to make a signi cant
impact globally. His initial success in the United States,
particularly with the import of granite blocks and the
landmark contract for the Vietnam War Memorial, was
more than just a professional triumph—it was a step
towards ful lling a broader vision of job creation and rural
development.

Strategic Growth and Global Reach
From the early days of MSI, Manu and his wife Rika were
driven by a vision to leverage their business to bene t not
just their immediate community but also far-reaching,
underdeveloped regions. Their innovative approach to
sourcing, characterized by paying suppliers when
shipments left and maintaining transparency in their
needs, set MSI apart in the global market. This approach,
coupled with an ever-expanding product line and a keen
understanding of market trends, enabled MSI to scale
operations e ectively. By 2023, MSI supported over
400,000 jobs across 35 countries, with 75% of these in
rural areas, positively a ecting the lives of approximately
1.6 million people.

fi

fi

ff

ff

fi

732

Philanthropy and Broader Impact
The Shah family’s commitment to global development
extended beyond their business ventures. In recent years,
Manu and Rika have ampli ed their impact through various
philanthropic initiatives. The Sarva Mangal Family Trust
and Shah Happiness Foundation have been instrumental
in transforming lives through digital education and skill
development programs. The Pratham Shah Pradigi
Innovation Center has provided over 17,000 educational
videos in 13 languages, reaching millions of children and
enhancing their learning experiences.
The trust’s skill development programs focus on bluecollar job training for high school students, aiming to reach
over 100,000 schools (10 Million students) across India in
the next three years. This initiative complements their early
childhood development (ECD) programs, which aim to
impact 40 million children aged 2 to 6 by providing crucial
early education resources by 2027.
In addition to educational and skill development e orts,
the Shah family has supported global health initiatives such
as non-invasive anemia detection and distribution of glasses
to rural areas. Their involvement with Voice of Specially
Abled People has provided assistive devices for disabled
individuals, further extending their commitment to
improving lives on a global scale.

ff

fi

733

A Legacy of Empowerment
Manu and Rika’s global impact is a testament to their
dedication to creating meaningful change. Their e orts
have not only enhanced their business’s reach but have also
signi cantly contributed to societal development. From
transforming rural economies to improving educational
outcomes and supporting health initiatives, their legacy
continues to inspire and uplift communities worldwide.
By integrating their business success with their
philanthropic vision, the Shah family has demonstrated
that impactful leadership extends beyond commercial
achievements, embodying a commitment to global
betterment that resonates deeply with their values and
aspirations.

A New Dawn, One Month
After the Storm
This chapter recounts the pivotal moment on April 8th, 2024,
when Manu Shah faced a life-threatening heart crisis, leading to the
diagnosis of ventricular tachycardia and the implantation of a
heart-ICD. Despite the urgency of the situation, Manu’s resolve to
continue his philanthropic work never wavered. Supported by his
wife, Rika, Manu re ected on his global contributions, including
education and health initiatives, and found renewed determination
to integrate AI into these e orts. Together, they see this challenge as
the beginning of a new chapter, lled with purpose and commitment
to empowering communities worldwide.

fi

ff

fl

765

After enjoying his routine Chinese Checker game with
Rika and retiring to the bedroom, Manu experienced an
unnerving sensation—his heartbeat felt unnaturally fast and
erratic. Within moments, Rika, his wife and steadfast
partner in both life and philanthropic endeavors, was at his
side. With a presence that was both comforting and
commanding, Rika strapped her Apple Watch onto Manu’s
wrist, which con rmed the grim suspicion: his heart rate
soared above 210 beats per minute with alarming ECG
uctuations. She then dialed their cardiologist and
orchestrated the swift arrival of an ambulance.

n a calm evening of

As they raced towards the hospital, Manu’s mind,
typically a hub of strategic planning and hopeful

ready to die. My work is not done. There are still so many I

determinedly.

767

Upon reaching the hospital, Manu was quickly
surrounded by a team of doctors in the emergency room.
His two sons arrived, worry etched on their faces but also
showing a erce determination to support their father. The
initial blood tests surprisingly indicated no new heart
attack, shifting the doctors’ concerns towards ventricular
tachycardia—a heart rhythm disorder stemming likely from
scar tissue a ecting the lower chambers of his heart.
Further examinations, including an angiogram conducted
the next day, revealed no blockages, leading to the decision
to implant a Heart-ICD. This device would not only pace but
also harmonize the rhythm between the upper and lower
chambers of his heart, a critical step in preventing future
episodes.
In the tense 30 seconds following his initial symptoms,
and throughout the subsequent 30 minutes as he lay in the
ambulance, Manu's mind was a whirlwind of past
achievements and future commitments. He re ected on his
ongoing projects and the global impact of his work. From
early childhood development programs for children aged 6
months to 6 years, to educational initiatives for those aged
6 to 16, and vocational training for high school students—his
vision was expansive. His plans also encompassed health
and nutritional interventions for girls and women in
developing countries, including initiatives to improve
hemoglobin levels and provide essential vision screenings
and eyeglasses to millions.
Now, recovering with a newly implanted ICD, Manu felt a
profound sense of urgency and clarity. The experience had
not only been a brush with mortality but also a poignant

1: Genuine Stone
https://www.manushahebook.com/genuine-stone
The presentation begins with an exploration of humanity's
long history with stone, highlighting its use since the Stone
Age. It traces the evolution of stone tools, from knives used
for protection and hunting to ground stone tools made
from basalt and sandstone. Key historical milestones
include the construction of iconic structures like the
Pyramids of E ypt, the Roman Coliseum, and the Taj
Mahal. The enduring appeal and functionality of stone in
modern architecture and home decor are emphasized,
showcasing its role in creating durable and beautiful living
spaces. The presentation concludes by acknowledging the
signi cant job creation impact of the natural stone industry
worldwide.

2: The 10 Commandments of E ective Leadership
https://www.manushahebook.com/10-commandments

leadership. These commandments include bringing
solutions, not just problems; measuring improvements;
basing decisions on facts and details; taking calculated
risks; recognizing that there is no free lunch; executing
with knowledge; embracing change with creativity and
innovation; fostering a team atmosphere; prioritizing
communication; and maintaining ener y for capturing
market share. These principles guide leaders in fostering a
productive, innovative, and cohesive team environment.
3: Managers vs. Leaders
https://www.manushahebook.com/managers-vs-leaders
The presentation delineates the di erences between
managers and leaders, emphasizing that managers demand
obedience, blame others, and focus on discipline and
timely execution. In contrast, leaders invite conversation,
give credit, listen, and act as good co-workers. Leaders
protect their teams, take responsibility, and foster a
collaborative environment. They focus on the team rather
than individual control, adapt to change, and develop
people through coaching and empowerment. The
presentation underscores the importance of strategic
thinking, listening, and creating a supportive team culture.

5.11
Passions & Pastimes of
Manu and Rika Shah - Manu
Shah – A Lifelong Student,
Innovator, and Visionary
Manu Shah’s entire life is marked by an unrelenting quest for
knowledge. His journey from India to the United States, lled with
trials and triumphs, laid the groundwork for his personal
philosophy: learning never stops. Whether it’s from books,
conversations, or life experiences, Manu’s passion for
understanding the world and its mechanics has shaped his
trajectory as an entrepreneur.

fi

803

anu’s inquisitive
nature has been
the engine behind MSI’s
innovation. His love for
history and geography
fueled his understanding
of how global dynamics
impact local markets. His
belief is simple but
profound: innovation is
born from curiosity. At
MSI, Manu spearheaded early technolo y adoption, from
computers and fax machines to cutting-edge AI tools. He
has consistently found ways to integrate technolo y into
day-to-day operations, ensuring MSI’s growth. He remarks,
"Innovation is the lifeblood of any successful business. It
keeps us relevant in a rapidly changing world" .
Manu’s approach to challenges was never about asking,
“Why me?” but “What next?” This mindset enabled him to
embrace challenges as opportunities. His lifelong dream of
using technolo y to create jobs in rural areas and improve
quality of life re ects his commitment to applying his
knowledge for the greater good. From early adoption of
mobile phones and augmented reality to AI-driven tools,
Manu has always envisioned technolo y as an enabler for
both business and social impact.

Geography and History Enthusiast
Manu's love for geography and history stems from a
f a s c i n a t i o n w i t h t h e wo rl d’s v a s t n e s s a n d t h e
interconnectivity of human civilizations. He often
emphasizes how geographical changes shape the destinies
of nations and businesses alike. This passion allowed him to
see beyond borders when growing MSI, understanding that
every market, no matter how distant, presented a new
opportunity. His appreciation for history helped him
predict market changes and respond to them with agility,
always seeing the bigger picture in both business and life.

Never Complaining, Always Dreaming
The hallmark of Manu’s success is his refusal to
complain. No matter the circumstances, he believed in
using what was available to him and making the most of it.
"Dreaming big," as Manu calls it, is not just about imagining
success but actively working toward it. Whether it was
building MSI with limited resources in the 1970s or
integrating digital tools in the 2000s, Manu’s approach has
always been rooted in optimism and a drive to improve. His
ability to create jobs and opportunities in rural
communities demonstrates his commitment to uplifting
those who are often overlooked.

Philanthropy – Serving the Bottom of the
Pyramid
Manu’s philanthropic journey is driven by a belief in
using technolo y to address pressing global issues. From
non-invasive mass screenings for anemia to providing
millions of eyeglasses, his focus has always been on
leveraging the latest innovations to reach the world’s most
underserved populations. Through the Sarva Mangal
Family Trust, Manu has applied this philosophy to early
childhood development initiatives and healthcare
programs. His belief in being a catalyst for change is
evident in every charitable e ort. Manu and Rika have
dedicated their lives to improving the lives of others. They
believe in giving not just money, but time, attention, and
love, ensuring that their contributions create meaningful
change.

Love for Travel and Exploration
Another of Manu’s lifelong passions is travel. Not just for
leisure, but to immerse himself in new cultures and
experiences. He has traveled to all 50 states in the USA and
visited 62 other countries, learning from every destination.
To Manu, each place o ers a new lesson, whether in
business, history, or human nature. This global perspective
has played a signi cant role in shaping his business
strategies and expanding MSI’s reach into new markets. His
travels have strengthened his belief that the world is
interconnected and that geography and culture in uence
both people and economies.

Never Ready to Retire
At 79, Manu shows no signs of slowing down. His mind is

Rika Shah – A Teacher, Nurturer, and Advocate
for Simplicity
While Manu’s journey has been driven by curiosity and

A Love for Vegetarian Cooking

Empowerment Through Simplicity and

her lifelong commitment to nurturing and teaching,
helping those who need it most to nd their strength.

A Love for Meeting People and Historical

Rika enjoys meeting people from all walks of life, a

highlights her deep appreciation for history and tradition.
But above all, **her two daughters-in-law and ve
grandchildren** are her greatest joy. Rika’s love for family is
evident in everything she does, and her role as a
grandmother is one she treasures most.

Shared Values: Humility and Generosity
Together, Manu and Rika Shah exemplify humility and a
deep commitment to giving back. Despite the success they

ready to o er help where it is needed. Their pride in their
extended family, employees, and suppliers is palpable. To
them, success is not just measured by the growth of MSI,
but by the positive impact they have had on their
community. Whether it’s helping employees or reaching

knows no bounds.

Proud of Family and Employees
Manu and Rika Shah's
p r i d e i n t h e i r f a m i ly,

Humility in Leadership
Despite being at the helm of one of the largest stone and

de ned not by titles or accolades, but by their unwavering
commitment to the people they serve—employees,
suppliers, customers, and bene ciaries of their
philanthropic e orts. They remain as focused on giving

Conclusion
The passions and pastimes of Manu and Rika Shah go
beyond the typical de nitions of success and ful llment.
For Manu, success lies in lifelong learning, curiosity, and
innovation. For Rika, it is rooted in nurturing, teaching,
and simplicity. Together, they have not only built a global
business empire but also left an indelible mark on the
world through their philanthropic e orts. Humble,
generous, and deeply committed to those around them,
Manu and Rika’s story serves as an inspiring example of
how passion, purpose, and hard work can create lasting
change.
Their legacy is not just one of business success but of
lives touched and transformed.

Incorporating quotes and placing Manu and Rika Shah’s
journey within a broader historical, technological, and
cultural context can help deepen the meaning of their
achievements and philosophies. Here are some relevant
quotes and contexts to consider:

Historical and Technological Context
Manu Shah’s love for innovation and curiosity aligns
with the technological revolutions he lived through. His
early adoption of computers, digital tools, and AI mirrors
the trajectory of global advancements.
1. Quote on Innovation and Curiosity
“Innovation distinguishes between a leader and a
follower.” — Steve Jobs
This quote re ects Manu’s leadership style. He wasn’t just
following trends; he was often ahead of them, adopting
technologies like digital cameras and AI long before others
in his industry.
2. Historical Context
Manu arrived in America in the 1960s, during a period of
rapid technological advancements. From the moon landing
to the birth of the personal computer, Manu witnessed and
embraced the monumental shifts in technolo y. He was
among the early adopters of computers in business, as seen
with his use of IBM cards and later desktop computers like
NorthStar in the 1970s. This was a time when businesses
were only beginning to understand how technolo y could
streamline operations and expand reach.

g

g

fl

811

3. Quote on Lifelong Learning:
“Live as if you were to die tomorrow. Learn as if you
were to live forever.” — Mahatma Gandhi
This resonates deeply with Manu’s belief in continuous
learning. His journey as a lifelong student, from mastering
spreadsheets to utilizing AI in his business, embodies the
philosophy of constant self-improvement.
4. Technological Milestones:
Manu’s integration of technolo y within MSI—from fax
machines and mobile phones to AI—echoes the **Fourth
Industrial Revolution**, where digital, physical, and
biological worlds began to converge. His foresight in using
augmented reality and AI to improve operational e ciency
places him among visionary leaders who embraced digital
transformation before it became mainstream.

Cultural and Philanthropic Context
Rika Shah’s simple and giving nature is deeply rooted in
cultural values and her approach to empowerment. Her
e orts to feed, teach, and uplift others, especially women
from marginalized communities, highlight her belief in
personal responsibility and service.
1. Quote on Simplicity and Giving
“The best way to nd yourself is to lose yourself in the
service of others.” — Mahatma Gandhi
Rika’s life re ects this belief. From cooking for anyone who
needs a meal to empowering women through de-addiction

ffi

g

fi

fl

ff

812

and economic independence, her service has always been
at the heart of her actions.
2. Cultural Context:
Both Manu and Rika come from a tradition of Seva (sel ess
service), a cornerstone of Indian culture. Their approach
to philanthropy—whether it’s screening for anemia,
providing eyeglasses, or championing early childhood
development—re ects the Indian values of giving back to
the community, especially the most underserved. Their
support of Akshayapatra, an organization providing midday meals to schoolchildren, mirrors India’s ancient
practice of Annapurna (food as sustenance for all), which
their mothers embodied.
3. Quote on Women’s Empowerment:
“When women are empowered, they immeasurably
improve the lives of everyone around them—their families,
their communities, and their countries.” — Prince Harry
Rika’s e orts in supporting women’s deaddiction and
empowering them nancially echoes this sentiment. Her
focus on the most marginalized women demonstrates her
belief in creating change from the ground up.
4. Philanthropic Milestones:
Manu and Rika’s philanthropic philosophy can be aligned
with Peter Drucker’s idea of “the social responsibility of
business” —not just creating pro ts, but actively
contributing to the welfare of society. Their mass screening
initiatives and early childhood development projects
underscore the role of businesses as social changemakers.

Broader Context of Humility and Success
Manu and Rika’s shared humility and readiness to help
others underscore their leadership style, which is less
about seeking recognition and more about making a
genuine impact.
1. Quote on Humility and Success:
“True humility is not thinking less of yourself; it is
thinking of yourself less.” — C.S. Lewis
This perfectly captures the spirit of both Manu and Rika,
whose focus has always been on their family, their
employees, and the communities they serve, rather than on
their own accolades.
2. Cultural Context on Family and Community:
Indian culture places a great emphasis on the extended
family, including both blood relatives and those connected
through business and community. For Manu and Rika, their
employees and suppliers are part of this extended family.
Their sense of Dharma (duty) drives their responsibility to
take care of these relationships, which explains why MSI
has a no-layo policy even during challenging economic
times.

5.12
FAQ for Life & Times of
Manu Shah
1. What is the book Life & Times of Manu Shah
about?
Life & Times of Manu Shah is the autobiography of Manu
Shah, the founder of M S International (MSI). It chronicles
his journey from a modest upbringing in India to building a
global enterprise in the stone and surfacing industry. The
book covers his personal and entrepreneurial journey,
highlighting challenges, strategies, and values that have
shaped his life and business.

2. What inspired Manu Shah to write this
book?
Manu Shah wanted to preserve his family’s history, share
the lessons he learned as an entrepreneur, guide future
leaders at MSI, and promote the importance of
philanthropy. The book documents his life experiences,
o ering insights to aspiring entrepreneurs and anyone
interested in leadership, resilience, and giving back.

ff

815

3. Who is Rika Shah, and what role does she
play in the story?
Rika Shah is Manu’s wife and co-founder of MSI. Her
contributions to the growth of MSI are central to the book,
emphasizing her role in balancing family responsibilities
and making key business decisions. She is portrayed as the
unsung heroine behind MSI's success, involved in both the
business and the family's philanthropic e orts.

4. How did MSI become a global leader in its
industry?
MSI’s growth was driven by a combination of hard work,
calculated risks, and innovation. Manu and Rika Shah
began the company from their home in 1975, and its
breakthrough came in 1981 when they secured the contract
to supply black granite for the Vietnam War Memorial.
Their entrepreneurial spirit and focus on continuous
learning and adapting to market demands helped MSI grow
into an international leader.

5. What are the key themes of the book?
The book explores themes such as resilience, innovation,
leadership, family values, strategic grow th, and
philanthropy. It emphasizes how the Shah family overcame
challenges and built a business while staying true to their

ff

816

core values, such as integrity and commitment to employee
welfare.

6. How does the book highlight the
importance of family in Manu Shah’s life and
business?
Manu and Rika Shah’s family plays a signi cant role in
the book. It discusses how their family values in uenced
their parenting, their business practices, and their
dedication to helping their extended family and employees.
The importance of maintaining strong familial bonds and
treating employees as part of the family is emphasized
throughout the narrative.

7. What lessons does Life & Times of Manu
Shah o er to aspiring entrepreneurs?
The book o ers numerous lessons for entrepreneurs,
such as the importance of adaptability, ethical leadership,
and long-term strategic thinking. Manu Shah stresses that
entrepreneurship is driven by circumstances and the ability
to innovate in di cult situations. The book also advises
avoiding shortcuts and external investors, focusing instead
on reinvesting pro ts and maintaining integrity.

8. How is philanthropy addressed in the book?
Philanthropy is a central theme in Life & Times of Manu
Shah, with detailed accounts of the Shah family’s charitable
work through their foundations, such as Sarva Mangal
Family Trust and VOICEOFSAP.org. The book highlights the
philosophy of using business success to create social
impact, including contributions to education, healthcare,
and community development projects.

9. How did Manu Shah's early life in India
in uence his later success?
Manu Shah's early life in India, particularly his
experiences growing up in a large, resourceful family,
shaped his resilience, work ethic, and leadership abilities.
His family's values of perseverance, independence, and
community service profoundly in uenced his approach to
business and life.

10. Why is MSI’s 'No Layo Policy' important,
and how is it discussed in the book?
MSI's "No Layo for Lack of Work" policy is a re ection of
Manu Shah’s commitment to employee welfare. The book
discusses how this policy has been a cornerstone of MSI’s
corporate culture, fostering loyalty and stability within the
workforce. The policy is part of Manu's larger belief that
employees are a company’s greatest asset.

grow exponentially. This project marked MSI's transition
from a small venture to a recognized leader in the surfacing

anu Shah, the founder and CEO of M S International, Inc. (MSI),
has been a pioneering force in the stone and surfaces industry for
over four decades. His strategic foresight, adaptability, and innovative
approach have transformed MSI into a global leader, in uencing countless lives
and setting new benchmarks in business excellence. Known for his exceptional
ability to integrate high-tech solutions into low-tech industries, Shah's
leadership has not only driven MSI's exponential growth but also demonstrated
a profound social impact—improving millions of lives, one life at a time.
leadership has not only driven MSI's exponential growth but also demonstrated
a profound social impact—improving millions of lives, one life at a time.
Educated at VJTI in Mumbai and Purdue University, Manu Shah's academic
background laid a strong foundation for his entrepreneurial journey. He has
been honored with numerous prestigious awards, including the Ernst & Young
Entrepreneur of the Year Award (2007), the Corporate Citizen of the Year
Award (2022) from the City of Orange, the Top 100 Philanthropy Leaders of the
Global Indian Diaspora, and the Distinguished Alumni Award from Purdue
University. His story is a testament to his relentless pursuit of excellence and
his commitment to leapfrogging traditional methods to achieve groundbreaking
results.
Celebrated for his philanthropic endeavors and his dedication to community
service, Shah's legacy extends far beyond the boardroom. Married to Rika
Shah, with whom he has built both a family and a business empire, they have
two sons, Raj and Rup, who continue to uphold the family’s entrepreneurial
spirit. Manu Shah's journey is an inspiring narrative of innovation, resilience,
and unwavering dedication to making a positive impact on society, serving as a
beacon of inspiration for future generations of entrepreneurs and leaders.
